    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app',

  <span id="freeText11264336366669235116" style="display:none"><i>A simple but forgotten truth: Where harbingers of death appear, the morgues will soon be full.</i><br /><br />Angie Dovage can tell there’s more to Reece Fernandez than just the tall, brooding athlete who has her classmates swooning, but she can’t imagine his presence signals a tragedy that will devastate her small town. When something supernatural tries to attack her, Angie is thrown into a battle between good and evil she never saw coming. Right in the center of it is Reece—and he’s not human.<br /><br />What’s more, she knows something most don’t. That the secrets her town holds could kill them all. But that’s only half as dangerous as falling in love with a harbinger of death.</span>

<div id="review_2085674162" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2085674162" />
    <a title="Melanie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie"><img alt="Melanie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577914102p2/3030788.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2085674162?book_show_action=true">Aug 08, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melanie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melanie" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie">Melanie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=shifters">shifters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=read-in-2017">read-in-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2085674162" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2547119141728798051"><i>ARC provided by the publisher via Netgalley in exchange for an honest review.</i><br/><br/>📖💗: You can win an exclusive Book Nerd T-Shirt by being one of the first 100 people to leave a review of <i>Black Bird of the Gallows</i> by Meg Kassel on Amazon! Enter to win <a href='https://docs.google.com/forms/d/e/1FAIpQLSd3uMaYuvL_xl33iPtvATbYGdcRVnlpt9U7-dAL7wV6QIRA7w/viewform' rel='nofollow noopener'>Here</a>!<br/><br/>📖💖: Three people can also win a <i>Black Bird of the Gallows</i> canvas tote bag (11“x14”) which includes a custom made crow pendant and ball chain, bookmark and stickers, $10 Amazon Gift Card (INT) Enter to win <a href='https://www.rafflecopter.com/rafl/display/1cb554951159/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Here</a>!<br/><br/>📖💕: And check out the rest of the revie</span>
  <span id="freeText2547119141728798051" style="display:none"><i>ARC provided by the publisher via Netgalley in exchange for an honest review.</i><br><br>📖💗: You can win an exclusive Book Nerd T-Shirt by being one of the first 100 people to leave a review of <i>Black Bird of the Gallows</i> by Meg Kassel on Amazon! Enter to win <a href="https://docs.google.com/forms/d/e/1FAIpQLSd3uMaYuvL_xl33iPtvATbYGdcRVnlpt9U7-dAL7wV6QIRA7w/viewform" rel="nofollow noopener">Here</a>!<br><br>📖💖: Three people can also win a <i>Black Bird of the Gallows</i> canvas tote bag (11“x14”) which includes a custom made crow pendant and ball chain, bookmark and stickers, $10 Amazon Gift Card (INT) Enter to win <a href="https://www.rafflecopter.com/rafl/display/1cb554951159/" rel="nofollow noopener">Here</a>!<br><br>📖💕: And check out the rest of the reviews, interviews, and more from this blog tour <a href="http://www.chapter-by-chapter.com/tour-schedule-black-bird-of-the-gallows-by-meg-kassel-presented-by-entangled-teen/" rel="nofollow noopener">Here</a>!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1505200548i/23897059._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Stay away from the bees.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><i>Black Bird of the Gallows</i> is a debut standalone paranormal YA romance that reads like a mixture of <i>Candyman</i> meets <i>The Birds</i> meets <i>Twilight</i>. (And I mean that mashup in the best way possible!)<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1505890235ra/23967795.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1500769188ra/23383557.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1505890234ra/23967794.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“The energy flows over me, fills me, and none of it feels tainted, contaminated by the darkness of my mother’s mistakes.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Angie Dovage lives in a small town in southwest Pennsylvania and is counting down the days of her senior year of high school, so she can finally graduate and escape the small town that won’t let her forget her childhood. She is living with her father, making music with her two best friends, and trying to ignore that past that still haunts her. That is, until a new boy moves in next door and makes her realize there may be more to her small sleepy town than anyone realizes. <br><br>Reece is not your regular human boy, but is also harboring a secret that will change Angie’s world forever. Together they are trying to uncover the fate of their small town, while also learning to trust one other and overcoming their own personal fears. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“If you had asked me a few weeks ago, I’d have said magic is impossible. Irrational. Just considering its existence in this world is insane. But I saw bees crawl out of a man’s mouth. I saw him change faces like pages of a book.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>This book has a dark and spooky vibe throughout its entirety. The writing is beautiful and for sure helps create this haunted aesthetic vibe, which I loved. This book feels and reads very much like a mystery thriller, even though it is for sure a paranormal romance. Also, I feel like the story itself was just super unique. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“I endured two centuries of horrors, and maybe it was all so I could be here with you. If my unnatural existence means nothing else, it means this. I get to be here, now, with you.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>I had a little problem with the romance in this book, and how fast and instant it seemed to be. The story later addresses this with more back content, but that addition just made me feel a little creeped out. I also felt like the ending was a little too easy and convenient for my liking, as well. But those were the only two issues I really had. Besides those, this was a really enjoyable read. <br><br>I do think it’s important to note that this book centers around death a lot. So, trigger warnings for talk of death, child abuse, and a minor plot point that surrounds a school shooting. Yes, this is a YA novel, but the nature of this book definitely deals with some dark subject matters, so please go into this book knowing that. <br><br>I completely recommend this, especially for a fun Halloween paranormal read! I really enjoyed Angie’s friendships with Deno and Lacey and then her parental relationship with her father. Also, I love that this is a standalone, because those are so unheard of nowadays, especially in the paranormal genre. This is a quick and easy read that would be super enjoyable for the fall season. And I will definitely read future books by Meg Kassel, because of this wonderful debut. <br><br><a href="https://meltotheany.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.twitter.com/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://meltotheany.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/meltotheany/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UC4RbHEg_fH6CewJrh_0xJ9g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="http://www.twitch.tv/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitch</a> <br><br><i>The quotes above were taken from an ARC and are subject to change upon publication.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="2547119141728798051" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1476739852" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1476739852" />
    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1476739852?book_show_action=true">Aug 31, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2018">read-2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1476739852" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6769370109528735343"><b>A story all about harbringers, evil bees, music and paranormal tropes that get deliciously shaken up?!?</b> I AM SO HERE FOR THIS. I so so enjoyed this one. It's pretty dark too, which...excuse me while I slither out of the darkness, but <i>yes please</i>. And the characters were winning, it had epic friendships, the catastrophes were terrifying...and EVERYTHING WENT HORRIBLY WRONG! Lovely!<br/><br/><b>It had a lot of paranormal tropes...and it totally mixed them up!</b> Like you know how the Hot Supernatural Boy comes int</span>
  <span id="freeText6769370109528735343" style="display:none"><b>A story all about harbringers, evil bees, music and paranormal tropes that get deliciously shaken up?!?</b> I AM SO HERE FOR THIS. I so so enjoyed this one. It's pretty dark too, which...excuse me while I slither out of the darkness, but <i>yes please</i>. And the characters were winning, it had epic friendships, the catastrophes were terrifying...and EVERYTHING WENT HORRIBLY WRONG! Lovely!<br /><br /><b>It had a lot of paranormal tropes...and it totally mixed them up!</b> Like you know how the Hot Supernatural Boy comes into town and the girl goes gooey-eyed and loses her brain? NOT SO HERE. And it threw the annoying alpha-male-will-protect-you vibe out and gave us <i>so much epic solidly good stuff.</i> I was just smitten.<br /><br /><b>And can we talk about Angie?! BEST heroine.</b> She totally just ruled this book with such a relatable and fun voice! Also she totally<br />a) acknowledged Reece was a Supernatural Hot Boy but also CREEPY AF<br />b) had interests ... like her life wasn't consumed just by a boy omg<br />c) she had GOOD SOLID FRIENDS whom she loved and trusted a lot!<br />d) sarcasm is a great coping mechanism! are you sad and anxious? SARCASM IT OUT<br />e) she had a good relationship with her dad aww!<br />f) sees a dog? loves the dog<br />g) ice cream &gt; everything else<br /><br />I'm just here for Angie appreciation until the crOWS GO HOME. (see what I did there??? omg I am on fire with wit tonight)<br /><br /><b>The paranormal factor was also BEST because it had magic and creepy creatures.</b> Here for this omg. I love that it focused on curses: harbringers particularly. It was kind of unique?! They had their own lore and myths! We get introduced to creepy ass Beekeepers who kind of vomit bees and sting people into madness and 1000% stan this also because I'm allergic to bees in general and think honey is evil. Finally. My opinions are recognised.<br /><br />I also love how it was about catastrophes, tragedy, death and loss and grief...<b>but also fully of morally grey characters instead of downright EVIL.</b> The curses were the badies here. The people who were cursed were pretty freaking terrifying, but it WAS out of their control and I like how the book explored that?! It made me hate the "villains" but also feel sorrrrry for them.<br /><br /><b>My real only problems are small, but I think worth quickly pointing out.</b><br />• I'm really tired of 'healthy eating' being the butt of a joke. Like Angie's dad is into fitness so it's a HUGE running joke how much she hates not having diary or having to eat gluten free blah blah laugh/laugh how fake it is. It's actually <i>not</i>. Just as someone with huge food allergies, it'd be nice to not be mocked for once. <br />• They do make fun of social anxiety which is saddening.<br />• And, just personally, I HATE the "uber protective dad" trope. Like "omg look at my daughter and I'll get out the shotgun" thing. It's too rooted in patriarchal ownership of women so hm.<br /><br /><b>But seriously!? SO MUCH TO LOVE. I had an amazing time reading this!</b> The plot was addictive, the pacing always excellent. It had heartfelt messages and relatable characters in amongst DEATH and DESTRUCTION. And I love that it talked about sadness and how deep it can run, and how desolation can so ruin you. It's not an ultimately sad book, but I like that it talks about it.<br /><br />A solid YES from me. !!</span>
  <a data-text-id="6769370109528735343" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2073418266" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2073418266" />
    <a title="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries"><img alt="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557144778p2/15335689.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2073418266?book_show_action=true">Sep 12, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" class="user" itemprop="url" name="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" href="/user/show/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries">destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=otp">otp</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=review-copies">review-copies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=owned-physical">owned-physical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2073418266" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7451362201811415561"><b>I would rather the first boy who makes my heart beat like this, who makes my senses come alive, be a normal, human one, but I shouldn't be surprised. "Normal" hasn't exactly defined much of my life.</b><br/> <br/>I loved the paranormal romance genre as a teen, but hadn't picked it up in a while, so when I was offered a copy of this book, I jumped at the chance - and I'm so glad that I did!<br/><br/>Angie is a really likable narrator; she's been through a lot of hell in her eighteen years, and she portrays it believably</span>
  <span id="freeText7451362201811415561" style="display:none"><b>I would rather the first boy who makes my heart beat like this, who makes my senses come alive, be a normal, human one, but I shouldn't be surprised. "Normal" hasn't exactly defined much of my life.</b><br /> <br />I loved the paranormal romance genre as a teen, but hadn't picked it up in a while, so when I was offered a copy of this book, I jumped at the chance - and I'm so glad that I did!<br /><br />Angie is a really likable narrator; she's been through a lot of hell in her eighteen years, and she portrays it believably with her anxiety and insecurities. She's just trying to keep her head down and survive high school when she meets Reece, and while she's instantly attracted to him, she's not willing to rush into anything until he explains a few things to her: like why he's frequently surrounded by the new murder of crows surrounding her town, or why a man with an ever-changing face seems to be unreasonably concerned with not only Reece, but now Angie as well.<br /><br />I appreciated it wasn't super insta-lovey (though towards the middle it feels a little rushed, but it's explained later and is pretty adorable), and I really loved the banter and tension between Angie and Reece. It feels a little cheesy at times, but in that really fun, dramatic style that I fully expect from the PNR genre.<br /><br /><b>I hold my breath and watch the crow glide away. It melts into the blackness, silent as a ghost. Lonely as the night. Dark as a boy's eyes.</b><br /><br />A few loose ends were left untied by the end, and I wouldn't have minded another 50-100 pages to dive into the magical world's history a bit more. There's some potential for <i>really</i> cool magical world-building, but the opportunity wasn't seized. I especially wanted more information on the Strawmen, a mythical creature who is a very powerful entity, but we never get to see more than a brief glimpse of.<br /><br />Altogether, this was a captivating romance and had some very tender moments. I had so much fun reading it, and I would highly recommend it to <i>anyone</i> who loves YA paranormal romance stories.<br /><br /><i>Entangled was kind enough to send me a free copy of this book for reviewing purposes, but in no way did it affect my opinions!</i><br /><br /><b>You can find this review (and more) on my blog <a href="https://howlinglibraries.com/2017/09/13/blackbirdofthegallows/" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>!</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="7451362201811415561" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2134634297" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2134634297" />
    <a title="Sophie &quot;Beware Of The Reader&quot;" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18451976-sophie-beware-of-the-reader"><img alt="Sophie &quot;Beware Of The Reader&quot;" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1424022406p2/18451976.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2134634297?book_show_action=true">Sep 27, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sophie &quot;Beware Of The Reader&quot;" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sophie &quot;Beware Of The Reader&quot;" href="/user/show/18451976-sophie-beware-of-the-reader">Sophie &quot;Beware Of The Reader&quot;</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18451976-sophie-beware-of-the-reader?shelf=the-bests">the-bests</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18451976-sophie-beware-of-the-reader?shelf=most-wanted-book-of-2017">most-wanted-book-of-2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2134634297" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15632874249891548200">
  <strong>
    5+stars
  </strong>
<br/><br/> <br/><br/>
  <strong>
    Like a huge wave Black Bird of the Gallows engulfed me in its magic world and did not release me before the last sentence was over. It left me ashore a little stunned and with starry eyes.
  </strong>
<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1471172536ra/20008212.gif' width='480' height='208' alt='rapunzel' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/> <br/><br/>Meg Kassel achieved the high feat of making me rediscover a genre that I've read often. No blazé reader here!<br/><br/> <br/><br/>-The concept was original with Harbingers and Beekeepers.<br/><br/>-The pace was just right not too rushed not too slow.<br/><br/>-The characters were endeering and relatable.<br/><br/>-The romance w</span>
  <span id="freeText15632874249891548200" style="display:none">
  <strong>
    5+stars
  </strong>
<br><br> <br><br>
  <strong>
    Like a huge wave Black Bird of the Gallows engulfed me in its magic world and did not release me before the last sentence was over. It left me ashore a little stunned and with starry eyes.
  </strong>
<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1471172536ra/20008212.gif" width="480" height="208" alt="rapunzel" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br> <br><br>Meg Kassel achieved the high feat of making me rediscover a genre that I've read often. No blazé reader here!<br><br> <br><br>-The concept was original with Harbingers and Beekeepers.<br><br>-The pace was just right not too rushed not too slow.<br><br>-The characters were endeering and relatable.<br><br>-The romance was swoony.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1506535653ra/24026383.gif" width="480" height="240" alt="rapunzel" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> <br><br>-Everything worked perfectly.<br><br> <br><br>
  <strong>
    But I gush and I haven't explained the story yet!
  </strong>
<br><br>Take a seventeen year old Angie living with her dad in a small old mining town. Angie has lived a life of neglect with her mom for years until some tragic event led her in her loving father's arms again.<br> Angie has bagage. She is loaded with traumatic memories but thanks to music and probably therapy she is one of the most sane teenagers I know. She lives happily with her dad and has two great nerd/musicians best friends.<br><br>Now introduce a new family moving in the haunted house next door. Haunted as some horrific events happened in the house and no one wants to live in this house anymore.<br><br>Of course Angie is curious about her new neighbors. <strong>And of course she'll look after her dad's binocular to have a better view. Certainly not to check the new extra gorgeous boy next door...</strong><br><br>No luck though as there is a lot of crows in the way. Crows multiplying for weeks. Crows with red eyes and bringing small trove to Angie. Weird you say?<br><br>Well add a mysterious man in a wool jacket and a changing blurry face and see if it gets weirder by the day.<br><br>Of course the new neighbor would be built and handsome and kind and...Angie is falling for Reece.<br><br>All would be well if Reece did not have a huge secret. And if Angie's town was not on the brink of a huge change.<br><br> <br><br>Ok I stop here for the plot.<br><br> <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1506535366i/24026343._SX540_.jpg" alt="" width="472" height="378" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br> <br><br>
  <strong>
    To make it short:
  </strong>
<br><br>-Reece was the perfect YA hero. The one to make you wish go back to your first crush. See what he told Angie and tell me if it does not make you fall hard for him:<br><blockquote>
  
    <strong>
      "The world reeks of death and pain, and you smell like life and joy and everything I can never have."
    </strong>
  
</blockquote><br>-Angie was the right mix between strong and flawed, caring and curious, beautiful but not ostentatious.<br><br>-The side kicks as in her best friends, her dad and Reece's family had just enough substance to help run the story smoothly.<br><br>-The fantasy creatures were a new and fresh concept.<br><br>-I love star crossed or doomed lovers.<br><br>-The romance was just swoony and had me all starry eyes. A little heart broken for them too.<br><br>-The ending was unpredictable and just..right.<br><br> <br><br>Books like this one are real treats for Fantasy YA lovers like me. <strong>So read it as it's one of my best 2017 books. It wil certainly not be my last Meg Kassel's.</strong><br><br>
  <strong>
    And buy the printed book as not only is the cover gorgeous but the insidd of the book is just as beautiful!!!
  </strong>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=netgalley-edelweiss">netgalley-edelweiss</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=r2r-read">r2r-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=read-2017">read-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=death">death</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2087071880" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15985487103737124456">(I received an advance copy of this book for free. Thanks to Entangled Publishing, LLC and NetGalley.)<br/><br/>This was a YA paranormal romance featuring a harbinger of death who could turn into a crow.<br/><br/>Angie was an okay character, and I understood how she didn’t like attention after being labelled a freak after the situation she had been in with her mother. Living in a van with a drug-addicted mother, and being taken away shortly before her mother overdosed was hard enough for her without all the unwante</span>
  <span id="freeText15985487103737124456" style="display:none">(I received an advance copy of this book for free. Thanks to Entangled Publishing, LLC and NetGalley.)<br /><br />This was a YA paranormal romance featuring a harbinger of death who could turn into a crow.<br /><br />Angie was an okay character, and I understood how she didn’t like attention after being labelled a freak after the situation she had been in with her mother. Living in a van with a drug-addicted mother, and being taken away shortly before her mother overdosed was hard enough for her without all the unwanted attention associated.<br /><br />The storyline in this was about Angie meeting Reece, her new next-door neighbour, and realising that something was off about him and the crows that were suddenly everywhere. Slowly she began to find out more about him, and after following him forced him to confess that he was a harbinger of death, and could turn into a crow! We also got a storyline about Beekeepers, paranormal beings which house bees, which sting people and turn them mentally unstable. The paranormal aspect of this book was done well, and the ideas were pretty unique, but I did find the pace a little slow for me, and it took me a while to get through it.<br /><br />The ending to this a little confusing for me, but things were wrapped up fairly well, and there was no cliff-hanger.<br />6.5 out of 10.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15985487103737124456" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2086906256" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2086906256" />
    <a title="Carrie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36817401-carrie"><img alt="Carrie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1415677371p2/36817401.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2086906256?book_show_action=true">Aug 15, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carrie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carrie" href="/user/show/36817401-carrie">Carrie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/34874469-black-bird-of-the-gallows">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36817401-carrie?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2086906256" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4331809730345608431">Angie Dovage is like most people would be, a bit curious as to who her new neighbors are and what they will be like. When Angie runs into Reece Fernandez at the bus stop her curiosity is piqued even more by the good looking strange boy. Angie takes it upon herself to follow Reece and find out just what is behind the mysterious new boy. <br/><br/>What Angie ends up finding about Reece would send most people running and screaming. Reece is not a normal human boy, he's a harbinger of death. When a death happ</span>
  <span id="freeText4331809730345608431" style="display:none">Angie Dovage is like most people would be, a bit curious as to who her new neighbors are and what they will be like. When Angie runs into Reece Fernandez at the bus stop her curiosity is piqued even more by the good looking strange boy. Angie takes it upon herself to follow Reece and find out just what is behind the mysterious new boy. <br /><br />What Angie ends up finding about Reece would send most people running and screaming. Reece is not a normal human boy, he's a harbinger of death. When a death happens Reece feeds off the energy of the dying due to a curse he's been living with for centuries. But Reece is not the only supernatural in town and Angie finds herself in danger with Reece vowing to protect her. <br /><br />The one thing that I would complain about with Black Bird of the Gallows is that starting off it definitely had that feel of let's check off all the young adult fantasy expectations. The beginning of the story had flashes of Twilight to it which had me wondering if I'd find any originality buried within the pages. Of course too that brings me to the warning of the instalove that bother a lot of people since it's a typical oh the new boy is cute start but eventually there are more reasons added to the relationship. <br /><br />Thankfully the story of the battle between good and evil within the pages of this one did bring a bit of newness to it which made this one an interesting read. After reading this one I'll certainly be looking at crows and bees a bit differently so the author certainly got a bit creative with the supernatural side of the story which ended up making this one worth the read instead of just checking off what is expected in a young adult novel. <br /><br />I received an advance copy from the publisher via NetGalley.<br /><br />For more reviews please visit <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://carriesbookreviews.wordpress.com/">https://carriesbookreviews.wordpress....</a><br /><br /></span>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2103141299" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2103141299" />
    <a title="Alyssa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8472395-alyssa"><img alt="Alyssa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500935920p2/8472395.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2103141299?book_show_action=true">Aug 24, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alyssa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alyssa" href="/user/show/8472395-alyssa">Alyssa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8472395-alyssa?shelf=2017-releases">2017-releases</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2103141299" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5087789178967028016">4.5 stars. Very, very good. =)<br/><br/><br/><br/>***<a href='http://eaterofbooks.blogspot.com/2017/08/review-black-bird-of-gallows-by-meg.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Review posted on The Eater of Books! blog</a>***<br/><br/>Black Bird of the Gallows by Meg Kassel<br/>Publisher: Entangled Teen<br/>Publication Date: September 5, 2017<br/>Rating: 4 stars<br/>Source: Review copy sent by the publisher<br/><br/>Summary (from Goodreads):<br/><br/>A simple but forgotten truth: Where harbingers of death appear, the morgues will soon be full.<br/><br/>Angie Dovage can tell there’s more to Reece Fernandez than just the tall, brooding athlete who has her classmates swooning, but she can’t imagine his</span>
  <span id="freeText5087789178967028016" style="display:none">4.5 stars. Very, very good. =)<br /><br /><br /><br />***<a href="http://eaterofbooks.blogspot.com/2017/08/review-black-bird-of-gallows-by-meg.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Review posted on The Eater of Books! blog</a>***<br /><br />Black Bird of the Gallows by Meg Kassel<br />Publisher: Entangled Teen<br />Publication Date: September 5, 2017<br />Rating: 4 stars<br />Source: Review copy sent by the publisher<br /><br />Summary (from Goodreads):<br /><br />A simple but forgotten truth: Where harbingers of death appear, the morgues will soon be full.<br /><br />Angie Dovage can tell there’s more to Reece Fernandez than just the tall, brooding athlete who has her classmates swooning, but she can’t imagine his presence signals a tragedy that will devastate her small town. When something supernatural tries to attack her, Angie is thrown into a battle between good and evil she never saw coming. Right in the center of it is Reece—and he’s not human.<br /><br />What's more, she knows something most don't. That the secrets her town holds could kill them all. But that’s only half as dangerous as falling in love with a harbinger of death.<br /><br />What I Liked:<br /><br />I'd been looking forward to reading this book for quite some time, ever since a description was released. It has been a high-priority read for me, and a high-priority publication for Entangled. I had hoped that my expectations were not too high and I wouldn't be disappointed. I had nothing to worry about. This stunning debut is dark, imaginative, and enthralling, worth every bit of attention and hype it has received.<br /><br />In this story, Angie Dovage's world is turned to chaos, and it starts with crows. It has been years since anyone bought the neighboring house, but one day, a family moves in. Angie's new neighbors are a little strange, especially the teenage boy who is in many of her classes. What's even stranger is the arrival of many crows - and bees. There is more to Reece Fernandez, there is more to the crows who follow him - and Angie - and there is more to the bees. Angie finds herself in the midst of a supernatural war between the cursed Beekeeper and the harbingers of death. The town of Cadence is marked, and there can only be one outcome: death.<br /><br />From the start, I was hooked and I couldn't stop reading. There was no chance of me putting down the book until I finished. Kassel's writing and the flow of the story made it easy to get sucked into the story and lose track of time. I was never bored, so there was no worry about DNFing.<br /><br />I was a little surprised when I connected with Angie almost right away! She is a bit of a social outcast in her high school, due to something in her past surrounding her mother. But she is very gifted with music, and is a DJ at a club on weekends. She is smart and talented and a hard worker. She is also so strong and resilient, especially with everything she went through with her mother.<br /><br />I liked how that was revealed incrementally (what happened with Angie's mother). The first time you realize something is different about Angie's parental life, it's just this one phrase, a few words. The author slowly reveals parts of Angie's past. I love how the author ties it all together by the end. <br /><br />Reece is the male protagonist and I absolutely adored him. He is more than a swoony love interest (though he definitely is that). He's sweet and thoughtful, and occasionally he has broody moments, and protective moments, and a whole bunch of selfless moments. Reece is by no means a perfect guy, but he is very smart and full of worldly knowledge, so he understands certain things better than most. I liked him a lot and I thought he was a great character opposite Angie.<br /><br />There were many lovely secondary characters worth mentioning. Angie's dad is such a cool guy; he is fairly well-off, after a lot of hard work. He loves Angie so much and has a great relationship with her. He's a single dad, but he is really slaying the parenting thing. Here is an excellent example of a healthy parent-child relationship in YA lit - he is there, in his kid's life, and he isn't oblivious or always working. <br /><br />And then there are Angie's friends, Deno and Lacy. They are wonderful friends, so supportive and loyal. I also love that they each have a thing for each other - such a cute slow-burn almost-romance happening there. But mostly I was happy to see a great friendship between the three of them. <br /><br />Reece's family isn't as present as the other characters (and with good reason), but they are a wonderful family as well. I especially liked Reece's mom and really wished something could have happened between Reece's mom and Angie's dad!<br /><br />I loooooved the romance between Reece and Angie. They meet and the attraction begins, but it takes more than that for them to fall for each other. The interest is there, but the feelings start to build as the story goes. Kassel packs this book with plenty of Reece/Angie interactions, and there are a number of yummy swoons too. The romance progressed at a good pace, not too insta-love-y but not too slow either. I loved watching these two interact!<br /><br />The story is very action-packed and fast-paced, though not in an overwhelming way. The beginning of the book is more focused on Angie trying to figure out what is going on with the crows, the bees, Reece, and this creepy guy (who is revealed to be the villain). Then, when things are revealed to her, the real danger begins. The creepy buy - the Beekeeper - is intent on hurting Reece, and he'll go through Angie to do so. The "why's" and the "how's" are explained!<br /><br />The ending is very exciting and it wraps up well. There is a HEA. I believe this book is a standalone and I'm all for it - the story ends in a great place. But I also wouldn't hate seeing another book to follow, though it would be cool for this book to remain as it is. I loved the story and will probably being saying this a lot in the future!<br /><br />What I Did Not Like:<br /><br />There isn't anything specific that I didn't like. However, I would have loved to understand a little better what happened to Angie at the very end, in terms of this one thing. I didn't have a great grasp of this one aspect - the story went from one chapter to the next, one scene to the next. I can't say more without being specific and spoilery but there is something about the ending that could have used a little more explanation.<br /><br />Also, I wouldn't have minded more from Reece and Angie in terms of their relationship! They were incredibly cute and lovely together.<br /><br />Would I Recommend It:<br /><br />Fans of YA paranormal romance, this is a book for you! I love this kind of story. I love this kind of romance. I would definitely reread this again and I highly recommend it. It is appropriate for younger teens and up, as it is low on "inappropriate" language, sex, and violence. Well, there is violence, but it isn't too graphic or gruesome. In any case, this book would be a great addition to any YA reader's shelf!<br /><br />Rating:<br /><br />4.5 stars. My default is to round down but this is most likely going to end up on at least 2017 favorites list of mine, regardless of the rating. I'll be looking out for more by this author for sure. This book is a one-of-a-kind debut that should be on everyone's radars!</span>
  <a data-text-id="5087789178967028016" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2120647789" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2120647789" />
    <a title="Schizanthus Nerd" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52870273-schizanthus-nerd"><img alt="Schizanthus Nerd" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588332751p2/52870273.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2120647789?book_show_action=true">Sep 11, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Schizanthus Nerd" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Schizanthus Nerd" href="/user/show/52870273-schizanthus-nerd">Schizanthus Nerd</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52870273-schizanthus-nerd?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52870273-schizanthus-nerd?shelf=kindle-food">kindle-food</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2120647789" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer587291641054018913"><i>Blackbird singing in the dead of night, take these broken wings and learn to fly</i> ... Sorry, I kept hearing this song each time I read the title and music does feature in the book so it's not <b>completely</b> out there ...<br/><br/>The first thing I absolutely have to address about <i>Black Bird of the Gallows</i> is that cover. If you want people to need to buy a book without even knowing what it's about, then it seems like L.J. Anderson from Mayhem Cover Creations is your go to person. I simply <b>adore</b> the cover design</span>
  <span id="freeText587291641054018913" style="display:none"><i>Blackbird singing in the dead of night, take these broken wings and learn to fly</i> ... Sorry, I kept hearing this song each time I read the title and music does feature in the book so it's not <b>completely</b> out there ...<br /><br />The first thing I absolutely have to address about <i>Black Bird of the Gallows</i> is that cover. If you want people to need to buy a book without even knowing what it's about, then it seems like L.J. Anderson from Mayhem Cover Creations is your go to person. I simply <b>adore</b> the cover design and use of colour. I want a huge framed print of this cover artwork for my wall so I can constantly admire it.<br /><br />Now, where was I? Oh, the book. I really enjoyed it. What was it about? The birds and the bees, but not the way you're thinking!<br /><br />Angie has had it tough, spending a large part of her upbringing living in a van or at random mens' places with her drug addicted mother. While she's still haunted by her past, she now lives with her father, one of the most adorably sweet fathers I've come across in real life or the other real life (books). She has great friends, Lacey and Deno, and her very own secret identity as Sparo, a DJ in a nightclub.<br /><br />The house next door has been vacant since a tragedy made it impossible to sell. However, one day a moving truck appears and lo and behold, Angie spies (literally, through binoculars) the new cute boy moving in next door with his family. Mystery cute boy with the dark eyes isn't what he appears to be and as Angie gets to know him, she learns he's not quite as human as he looks, and apparently he looks really, really good.<br /><br />I loved the whole premise of this story. I'm a sucker for anything mythological so naturally I was drawn in by the origin stories of the tortured harbingers and Beekeepers. I wanted to know more about them though and I definitely wanted a backstory for the Strawmen. I'd love to read something from all of their perspectives that shed more of a light on them. Plus there's indications there are other entities/creatures/part human part something else types in this world and I want all the details about them as well.<br /><br />I had two favourite characters in this book. Rafette, who we spend a considerable amount of the book running from or on the lookout for, is someone I really empathised with. I found myself seeing the story from his point of view and didn't view him as a baddie at all. Maybe it's partly due to the soft spot I have for bees but my heart broke for Rafette and the pain he's endured in his life. I need to know so much more about him! And best friend Lacey ... supportive, intuitive and loving, yet willing to bash her best friend over the head with a golf club if that's what it takes to keep her safe. I loved Lacey!<br /><br /><i>Tissues Used</i>: 0, which surprised me as I came prepared. Although my icy cold heart experienced somewhat of an earthquake, none of the cracks melted into tears.<br /><br /><i>Food craved during reading</i>: Pancakes. Oh, they sounded so delectably droolworthy.<br /><br /><i>Something I thought would be important to remember when reading or rereading</i>: The names and stories of those you don't think will come back into the story. I found sections of this book to be in the 'six degrees of separation' category where peoples' stories linked together like one big crow shaped jigsaw puzzle. Prepare to get halfway through the book and go 'oh, I remember them!'<br /><br /><i>Now for the niggles</i>:<br /><br />* A minor thing, sure, but what's Reece's real name?<br /><br />* The insta-love frustrated me along with the whole 'our love is destined to be doomed and we'll both be miserable for all of eternity or for as long as we live (whichever is applicable) so we shouldn't be together. But first, let's kiss some more'.<br /><br />* Reece telling Angie that he's been in love with her since they were six. Now, this would have been worthy of an aww if not for the fact that <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[he would've been about 190, give or take a few years, at that stage which kind of morphed my aww into eww! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br /><br />* The whole thing about the big 'event' when loved ones are being searched for. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[When they all meet up at Angie's house after being separated did Angie not wonder or bother to ask Deno if his parents were alive or dead? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />* You know the whole horror movie girl victim/heroine who is always running up the stairs when she should be running out the door? I had that frustration with Angie. I kept wanting to yell at her to just <b>leave</b>! You can't say she didn't have ample warning time, yet she still managed to wind up caught up in the 'event' like everyone else. What use is fair warning if you don't listen, sweetheart?<br /><br />So, my rating. If I didn't have this many niggles, the writing would've deserved ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️. The niggles and frustration I felt while I was reading would usually have made it a ⭐️⭐️⭐️ but the writing was just so darn good. So I'm splitting the difference and giving this ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️.<br /><br />I received an ARC of this book from NetGalley (thank you so much to NetGalley and Entangled Publishing, LLC for the opportunity) in exchange for honest feedback. I will definitely read future books by Meg Kassel and I'll be stalking Amazon to grab my copy of the prequel novella when it's released in October 2017.</span>
  <a data-text-id="587291641054018913" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer11090036127382479899">So far so good. Not. Lured by the synopsis I began reading this book, and so far I find it to be full of topics:<br/><br/>- curious girl who feels atracted to the new guy who just moved into town and nest house<br/>- misterious brooding new guy who just moved into town<br/>- paranormal events: crows and flies flyring around, another misterious brooding guy who seems to be an enemy to the first<br/>- main girl ability to read on every little movement and glance of the new guy, never mind they have only talked for like te</span>
  <span id="freeText11090036127382479899" style="display:none">So far so good. Not. Lured by the synopsis I began reading this book, and so far I find it to be full of topics:<br /><br />- curious girl who feels atracted to the new guy who just moved into town and nest house<br />- misterious brooding new guy who just moved into town<br />- paranormal events: crows and flies flyring around, another misterious brooding guy who seems to be an enemy to the first<br />- main girl ability to read on every little movement and glance of the new guy, never mind they have only talked for like ten minutes, she is now an expert on everything "him"<br />- the attraction. O, the attraction! Comes out of nowhere, but o the attraction.<br />- hot girl from school, enemy of the main character who she bullies trying to seduce the new guy. Of course.<br />- and of course, one of the best friends is also an ex who sometimes creates some friction.<br /><br />Really? I used to love paranormal, and YA paranormal, but lately seems like it is so full of instalove, instaromance, insta attraction, insta high school recipe that it is dishearting. Will keep on reading because the prose is good and want to see if there is more to the book than just topics (which I believe could be).<br /><br />Aaaand... sadly I am done. I can't keep on reading this book. The "now I talk to you and now I don't but we always seem to be doing this on and off thingie" between the two main characters is just more than I can take besides all that I summed up before. <br /><br />It is a pity because the book shows promise and is very well written, but judging by the synopsis I thought I was going to read some kind of urban scyfi and not some YA "love me-love not and here I am to save your life while being esquive and aloft" kind of thing.<br />While the narrative is great the characters are more on the plain side (for me they never went far from the archetypical ones), but I think the author shows promise. And probably someone who is more into this kind of book would love it.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11274497889149385985">Thank you so much to Entangled and NetGalley for allowing me to read and review this AWESOME paranormal treat by Meg Kassel! Wow, this was so different from anything else I've read lately and I really loved Meg Kassel's originality in creating this supernatural world and plot elements. <br/><br/>Angie hasn't had the easiest past with a neglectful mother, and now lives with her father. When a new family moves in next door, into a house where there was a grisly murder, she's immediately curious about their </span>
  <span id="freeText11274497889149385985" style="display:none">Thank you so much to Entangled and NetGalley for allowing me to read and review this AWESOME paranormal treat by Meg Kassel! Wow, this was so different from anything else I've read lately and I really loved Meg Kassel's originality in creating this supernatural world and plot elements. <br /><br />Angie hasn't had the easiest past with a neglectful mother, and now lives with her father. When a new family moves in next door, into a house where there was a grisly murder, she's immediately curious about their teenage son, Reese. Of course, as we can expect, things don't turn out to be quite what they seem with Reese, and Angie soon finds herself drawn in to a super-creepy world inhabited by crows and beekeepers. <br /><br />I loved the chemistry between Reese and Angie. Angie is independent enough that her entire life doesn't go by the wayside over Reese, and their outlook on the reality of what's going on makes their relationship refreshing and enjoyable. The paranormal side of what's going on is at times... well... creepy. I don't want to give too much away. But definitely not straight up Edward Cullen "you're my heroin" romantic. And I was completely okay with that because I liked the way it added conflict. <br /><br />This was very well-paced, and the world-building was nicely done, too. Just a very enjoyable read. <br /><br />Disclaimer: I received a free copy of this book from the author.<br /><br />Please excuse typos. Entered on screen reader.</span>

<div id="review_2086729756" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2086729756" />
    <a title="Natshane" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3422972-natshane"><img alt="Natshane" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1491838445p2/3422972.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2086729756?book_show_action=true">Aug 25, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Natshane" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Natshane" href="/user/show/3422972-natshane">Natshane</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3422972-natshane?shelf=arc">arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2086729756" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10417155987040027278">Meg Kassel's debut novel was packed with thrill, romance and a chase unlike any other. Delve into the world of paranormal and be prepared for the rush as the author delivered a gothic horror novel that is both thrilling and chilling in this original story of ancient mythical creatures and the battle of good versus evil - featuring the <i>
  <b>harbingers of death. </b>
</i><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1494171964ra/22691086.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>Angie Dovage is a survivor of a childhood horror story that made her a victim of the rumors headlining the news. Now that she lives with </span>
  <span id="freeText10417155987040027278" style="display:none">Meg Kassel's debut novel was packed with thrill, romance and a chase unlike any other. Delve into the world of paranormal and be prepared for the rush as the author delivered a gothic horror novel that is both thrilling and chilling in this original story of ancient mythical creatures and the battle of good versus evil - featuring the <i>
  <b>harbingers of death. </b>
</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1494171964ra/22691086.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Angie Dovage is a survivor of a childhood horror story that made her a victim of the rumors headlining the news. Now that she lives with her dad, next to a house with the history of a family massacre, you can't blame her for being curious when the new family in town, the Fernandezes moved in into the house that has been vacant since the tragedy. And that includes stalking a particularly handsome young man, Reece, with her dad's binoculars. But the athletic and charming teen that is slowly taking over her heart is holding back a grave secret, one that not only threatens to ruin their newfound relationship but also destroys the very people she loves - can you fall in love with a harbinger of death? <br><br><i>
  <b> "The world reeks of death and pain, and you smell like life and joy and everything I can never have."</b>
</i><br><br>The author takes forbidden romance to a whole new level. I am incredibly impressed with the storyline, albeit predictable, the writing was enchanting and pulled me in from the start! I am so over forbidden romance ever since my Twihard years, but the intense chemistry between Angie and Reece was hard to ignore and even harder to not fall in love with. <br><br>Angie is an independent heroine that you just can't help but look up to. Given what she endured in her past, I loved the fact that she is discovering herself in this book and that she is brave enough to stand up for herself and own her decisions. Which brings me to my favorite character, Reece. Unlike the typical alpha male, Reece does not dictate or in any way forces Angie into making decisions that favor himself. Even when disaster strikes, he does not just sweeps in and save the day - a harbinger of death and all. <br><br>There are so many things about the book that I fell in love with - the dynamics of Angie's friendship with Deno and Lacey, Angie's relationship with her father, uncovering the mystery behind the ancient curse and the whole idea of beekeepers and harbingers, it was the ending that made me <i>almost</i> cried happy tears. From the start to the finish line, it was definitely a helluva roller coaster!<br><br><i>Thank you Entangled Teen and the author for the reviewing opportunity! I voluntarily read and reviewed an ARC of this book.</i> <br></span>
  <a data-text-id="10417155987040027278" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1687840437" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1687840437" />
    <a title="Melissa Souza" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/40579850-melissa-souza"><img alt="Melissa Souza" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1525391354p2/40579850.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1687840437?book_show_action=true">Sep 21, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa Souza" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa Souza" href="/user/show/40579850-melissa-souza">Melissa Souza</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40579850-melissa-souza?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40579850-melissa-souza?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40579850-melissa-souza?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40579850-melissa-souza?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40579850-melissa-souza?shelf=death">death</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40579850-melissa-souza?shelf=dark-atmosphere">dark-atmosphere</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1687840437" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16991784286649511151">3 stars!!!<br/><br/>When I first read the blurb for this book, I was pretty excited I have to say. But, unfortunately, this turned out to be a very average read for me. I guess it's because I found the story to have a usual YA elements. There wasn't enough of unique elements to push me to give it 4 or 5 stars. To get a clearer picture of why this was, let me unpack my reasons.<br/><br/>Firstly, I thought the book had potential to be awesome. I liked the concept of a world where there are these otherworldly beings t</span>
  <span id="freeText16991784286649511151" style="display:none">3 stars!!!<br /><br />When I first read the blurb for this book, I was pretty excited I have to say. But, unfortunately, this turned out to be a very average read for me. I guess it's because I found the story to have a usual YA elements. There wasn't enough of unique elements to push me to give it 4 or 5 stars. To get a clearer picture of why this was, let me unpack my reasons.<br /><br />Firstly, I thought the book had potential to be awesome. I liked the concept of a world where there are these otherworldly beings that took on animal spirits but could morph into humans. The idea of harbingers and beekeepers was interesting enough. I liked the backstory and history of how these beings came about and the curse that seems to be affecting them. The book has enough of a dark atmosphere to keep it engaging and the worldbuilding was mediocre at best.<br /><br />Secondly, the MC Angie is your average cliched YA girl. She has a passion for music, but can't seem to find herself. She doesn't really fit in and there's a mean girl whose on her case at school. I tend to find these kinds of MCs too boring, to be honest. There's no real depth of character. Yes, she's trying to be unique and she doesn't make overly stupid decisions but she's just meh. Add to this, she has some tragic past that she seems to be overcoming. I've read this character is scores of other YA books. However, I did like her relationship with her friends, her Dad and she seems like a level-headed girl. So, I couldn't necessarily dislike her. I just wanted more.<br /><br />Thirdly, the so-called "epic" romance was another cliche. She meets this handsome guy, Reece, and falls in love with him instantly because she feels a zing towards him. What? She barely even knows him. No one falls in love so instantly. Plus, she seems way too accepting when she finds out what he is. She doesn't even freak out once. I thought this was way too farfetched. Although, their romance is sweet. It lacks flaws and realness. Plus, it had no real feels. It was way too perfect. The author does add a touch of messiness to it but I felt it wasn't raw enough. <br /><br />Lastly, the overall plot had enough reveals to keep it interesting but the ending was very predictable and loose ends were tied in a neat bow. I was happy with it but it wasn't remarkable. There was plenty of action in the storyline which I appreciated. But as I said, everything fell into place way too perfect for my taste. The novel was structured really well and the facing was fast. There wasn't too much of irrelevant material which prevented it from being too tedious. That being said, I could see this book being darker with a more immersive world. I think it was too narrow and the overly sweet romance shadowed the grimmer elements. Maybe the author was going for a more hopeful approach. Either way, this novel is good for a one-time read and if you are looking for something to pass the afternoon. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16991784286649511151" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8296229929163798332">I liked this. I seriously appreciated a YA paranormal that did not include not one damn vampire or werewolf nor faerie!! <br/><br/>Side note: while I love a damn good faerie, I hate to admit that they’re starting to become the new vamps and weres of the last decade. <br/><br/>I freaking love crows. Or ravens. Or whatever. My inner goth adores them! So I was instantly drawn to Black Bird of the Gallows. Hello gorgeous cover! And hello creepy crow boys!<br/><br/>I loved the mc, Angie. She is this secretly badass electro-pop-te</span>
  <span id="freeText8296229929163798332" style="display:none">I liked this. I seriously appreciated a YA paranormal that did not include not one damn vampire or werewolf nor faerie!! <br /><br />Side note: while I love a damn good faerie, I hate to admit that they’re starting to become the new vamps and weres of the last decade. <br /><br />I freaking love crows. Or ravens. Or whatever. My inner goth adores them! So I was instantly drawn to Black Bird of the Gallows. Hello gorgeous cover! And hello creepy crow boys!<br /><br />I loved the mc, Angie. She is this secretly badass electro-pop-techno DJ on the mixing tables who works under the uber cool stage name of, “Sparo”. She’s so hipster she doesn’t even know it! I liked that. It felt unique. And it was fun getting an insight into that lifestyle and performance! <br /><br />I enjoyed this story. But unfortunately I didn’t love it. At times I got serious Bella and Edward vibes that I just couldn’t shake no matter how hard I tried to put Twilight out of my head and that kind of distanced me from everything. <br /><br />I didn’t feel emotionally attached to the characters which means I didn’t feel compelled into “page-gripping” during action scenes, which means I felt underwhelmed. <br /><br />As well, we’ve got some insta-love going on. And an *alllllllllmost* love-triangle like whew close one, but kudos for writing that nasty trope out. But all was forgiven because as I said in the beginning here, we need more paranormal reads outside of flipping vampires and werewolves! <br /><br />Looking forward to book 2 though....if it’s still going to happen. Mostly because a certain someone is 18 and has their own apartment..........woo woo! And if there is ever one thing I quest for more in the bookish world, it is a more NA than YA paranormal (sans effing vamps and weres), like perhaps this one with college age mc’s with a bit more college-age-shenanigans but written in a classy more subjective way like in YA?????!! Please tell me you get me?? <br /><br /><br />And here’s a rec along the same-ish lines as this read:<br /><br />If you enjoyed Black Birds of the Gallows then you’ll also enjoy Nevermore by Kelly Creagh!<br /><br />If you’re looking for something similar for your inner goth to keep you going until book 2 , I highly recommend the Nevermore trilogyby Kelly Creagh!!!</span>

<div id="review_2463020137" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2463020137" />
    <a title="Kristen Burns" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42225826-kristen-burns"><img alt="Kristen Burns" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1436601871p2/42225826.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2463020137?book_show_action=true">Jul 21, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristen Burns" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristen Burns" href="/user/show/42225826-kristen-burns">Kristen Burns</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42225826-kristen-burns?shelf=read-2018-books">read-2018-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42225826-kristen-burns?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42225826-kristen-burns?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42225826-kristen-burns?shelf=review-copy">review-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42225826-kristen-burns?shelf=other-supernatural">other-supernatural</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42225826-kristen-burns?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42225826-kristen-burns?shelf=paranormal-urban-fantasy">paranormal-urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42225826-kristen-burns?shelf=super-creative">super-creative</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2463020137" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10259779462502802483"><b>3.5 Stars</b><br/><br/><b>Review:</b><br/>*I received an ecopy of this book via YA Bound Book Tours. This has not influenced my review.*<br/><br/>This book had many of the typical YA trappings, but it also had a lot of uniqueness, and that was why I liked it.<br/><br/>I loved how this author took the idea of crows being harbingers of death and turned it into an actual supernatural creature. I have no idea if any author has ever done that before, but if they have, I've not come across it. It was unique and creative, and everything about the </span>
  <span id="freeText10259779462502802483" style="display:none"><b>3.5 Stars</b><br /><br /><b>Review:</b><br />*I received an ecopy of this book via YA Bound Book Tours. This has not influenced my review.*<br /><br />This book had many of the typical YA trappings, but it also had a lot of uniqueness, and that was why I liked it.<br /><br />I loved how this author took the idea of crows being harbingers of death and turned it into an actual supernatural creature. I have no idea if any author has ever done that before, but if they have, I've not come across it. It was unique and creative, and everything about the harbingers was interesting. As for the beekeepers, I don't know if that idea came from anything, but it was sure unique too. I won't go into detail about any of these things though since I think it's more fun to learn about them in the story.<br /><br />But as I said, there were some less unique things as well---high school cliques, something that felt a lot like instalove, and the brooding, tortured, centuries-old supernatural dating the teenage girl. Personally I could've done without some of these, but tropes are not inherently bad, and everyone likes different things.<br /><br />Plus, there were other things I enjoyed (in addition to the creativity of the supernatural elements). The writing and story had this great ominous feel. The main character was believable and likeable. The friendship she had with her two best friends and the relationship she had with her father were not the main focus but were sweet nonetheless. The DJ/music stuff was fun to read about. The disaster scenes were intense.<br /><br />Overall, this was a quick but ominous and enjoyable read, and I loved how unique the supernatural element was!<br /><br /><b>
  <a href="https://wp.me/p6ovgw-4iv" rel="nofollow noopener">Original Review @ Metaphors and Moonlight</a>
</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="10259779462502802483" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
